Title: TOTALLY NORMAL TWG: SKIDIDOOP - GAME OVER M&Ms WIN
Post by: eep on January 16, 2013, 01:35:24 PM
The gang goes to a perfectly normal restaurant for breakfast. And, like perfectly normal people they each order a perfectly normal bowl of skittles for breakfast. Everything is going wonderfully! No drama, no upsets, just everyone getting alo...

"Wait a minute," eep interjected. "Who put M&Ms in my skittles?" She stood up and looked menacingly around the room, one hand on the other, ready to remove the glove and slay the infiltrator. But no one owns up to it.

"Alright then," she growls. "I'll have to figure out which one of you did this myself. And in the meantime" - she looked down at her breakfast bowl, "I expect you to clean yourselves up before I get back."

All of you skittles shivered. How were you supposed to find the M&Ms, let alone get rid of them? You've never seen, heard, or said anything before, let alone destroyed another candy.

Nonetheless, you summon up your courage, and prepare to do what you know you must.

M&M GUARANTEE - no really i couldn't even make this up who does that sort of shit?
RULES - let's say 72 hour days and 24 48 hour nights because why not. If skittles get rid of all the M&Ms, they win; if M&Ms have a guaranteed path to eliminate the skittles, they win. change votes as many times as you like per day. In the event of a tie, the less active player will be lynched if there is a significant discrepancy (up to the host's judgment).
COLORS: optimized so that players believe they are going blind.
DEATH POSTING: Players may make 1 game-relevant post after death, but only the night after they die. All other (post-death-)posts must be game-irrelevant. Players may not post game-relevant information after their death.
PRIVATE COMMUNICATION: no player may communicate privately with another player without my express permission.

Had a fun idea about making it a bit more non-vanilla, so we'll stick it in there to see how it works. I mean disregarding the fact that this is actually a rainbow game anyways. To give you a hint, it relates to how the flavor plays out and avoiding any duplicates/made-up skittles.

Players:
1. penut
2. desu butt

4. d.agon

6. anim ktern

eep glares about the room, looking for any twitches that might reveal someone's guilt. At last, myctis speaks up.

"Hey, is this really such a big deal? I mean, you can just eat them individually or pick out the M&-"

A glove whizzes through the air and lodges itself in myctises face, slicing through his forehead and cheekbone as if they were hot butter. He makes a few last gurgling noises as blood begins to run down his neck, trickling down his arm and dripping rhythmically onto the floor. The bowl of skittles shifts, and something within it shatters. A powdery dust rises and disperses into nothingness.

You begin to feel something stirring within you, some strange sort of connection. You wonder what it is - sentience? the force? but you do not dwell long on either of these possibilities, because, as mere candies, you are not actually aware of them.

"Now then," eep chortled, "would anyone else like to offer some suggestions? Or will one of you own up?"

Let's try this puzzle.

Death Butt claims to know Mystic's color (purple) and has evidence that he knew this before last night. Death butt is Mystic's father, which is decent supporting flavor.

Quote from: death butt on January 22, 2013, 09:58:49 AM
There is nothing that says a 'spy' (I'm actually Mystic's father, not a spy, according to the flavor) can't be chocolate, though it seems to me rather pointless to tell a wolf someone's color, given they already know alignment.

My coming out as one didn't do much, but there wasn't much point in keeping it secret after Mystic died. The reason I went to the trouble of breadcrumbing it at all was so that if it did become important for me to reveal this information, I could prove that I knew it in the first day, before I could have used any night abilities.

Dieter is not claiming to be a spy. I personally don't find his analysis to be as incriminating as every else does. Actual color may not be useful (though may give hints - Mystic's potential purple could be relating to some metaphor or symbolism, like royalty, but guessing that kind of thing would be difficult), but mostly it's gonna be knowledge of color that helps.

In post 140, Dr. Agon wants to hear info from the aux roles. Could be rolefishing, but he supposedly has more info. Votes dietcar, then later says to wait for dietcar's information.

AngryNarwhal doesn't like Dietcar clearing Death Butt right away. That I can understand, though the Dietcar's reasons aren't necessarily malevolent.

Iron is a spy on Valex, according to himself. Could also be a wolf or a sorc in much the same way as Death Butt/Mystic. I understand Iron's reasoning about coming out with Valex's info, but I still think he could have waited. Would have been a gamble, but could have come out at a more useful time. Then again, I don't know when that would be.


So here's my analysis, looking at these people as best I can:

Death Butt and Iron both claim to be spies. There's no reason we can't have two spies. There's to spy/spied pairs at the moment: Death Butt/Mystic and Iron/Valex. The former seems more human (but by no means 100%) since Mystic got NK'd. Which might suggest an Iron/Valex wolf pair (which was the theory that my brain really liked, even though there's nothing really against either of them except the presence of Death Butt).

Lots of people don't like Dietcar, but I see nothing super-strong against him. AngryNarwhal seems to be operating on hunches and feelings. I don't really know what to think about the whole situation.

Death Butt's claim of purple for Mystic and Mystic's claim of not being purchasable conflict a bit. A fringe theory might be some odd breadcrumb like the purple=royalty idea, wherein you can't buy royalty. But I don't believe that.

Then there's a bunch of other people. At least one of them is probably chocolate. Peanut, anime, trientalis, and aj weren't mentioned at all in the above. I don't have a whole lot of info on any of them yet. I could maybe have a hunch, but I'd never be able to cite any evidence.

If Iron is a wolf, Valex probably is too. Though spy could be a wolf role, which would mean most of the information we have isn't all that useful. Ignoring that possibility (and, to a certain extent, including it), I actually want to go back to voting Iron though I'm probably something like 60% confident.

One more thing, and possibly further evidence for the theory:

Quote from: epplant on January 16, 2013, 01:35:24 PM
Had a fun idea about making it a bit more non-vanilla, so we'll stick it in there to see how it works. I mean disregarding the fact that this is actually a rainbow game anyways. To give you a hint, it relates to how the flavor plays out and avoiding any duplicates/made-up skittles.

Post by: eep on February 11, 2013, 04:11:01 PM
Valex suddenly slams his hands on the table.

"Wait! Everyone! Why are you doing this? We've been tricked! We're not so-hua"

He gets punched in the face, sending nasal bone up into his brain, killing him.

The rest of you gasp, suddenly, and then you realize:

"Wait a minute! We're not skittles or M&Ms. We're...we're people. Why did we believe...?"

You suddenly feel Mystic's blood, still splattered across your face. You turn to eep in horror, and everything seems frozen. You feel a shiver down your spine as you realize - time didn't stop. Only the dripping of the blood down Mystic's arm.

"How could you? What witchcraft was this? Did we really just..."

You turn around to take one last look at the carnage, before you all faint.

Game Over. M&Ms win.

Title: Re: TOTALLY NORMAL TWG: SKIDIDOOP - Day 5
Post by: eep on February 11, 2013, 04:32:40 PM
This game was obviously somewhat experimental, and I'm still not quite sure whether it had balance issues or skittles just didn't play very well. Early in making this game, I realized that there weren't that many colors of skittles (at least, not traditionally) and I though it would be neat to have a game with lots of spies and the wolves not knowing one another. It's another one of those slightly tricky situations where, had there been one less wolf, I think the game would have been pretty strongly stacked against wolves, but as was, it was possibly slightly in wolf favor. I imagine, though, that the game might have gone rather differently if more people had taken notice of this, in the first post:

Quote from: epplant on January 16, 2013, 01:35:24 PM
Had a fun idea about making it a bit more non-vanilla, so we'll stick it in there to see how it works. I mean disregarding the fact that this is actually a rainbow game anyways. To give you a hint, it relates to how the flavor plays out and avoiding any duplicates/made-up skittles.

It took a little while for people to start becoming suspicious of all the duplicates. Nonetheless, this was a sort of fun game to host because, for the first few days, the game was very, very close to swinging to one side or the other, but never quite made it there. And then it fell quite quickly.

Colors were actually totally randomized, but attached to roles, although there were a few somewhat funny coincidences (including mystic's "Tastes like purple") that I noticed afterwards.

I didn't think that allowing dieter to post the PMs would have quite the effect that it did (especially since it would be different from posting host PMs), but in hindsight that was a poor decision and I probably wouldn't do it again. Also, I knew that the game would have been over for skittles if dieter was lynched instead of dr.agon, but the opposite was not necessarily true. I had considered notifying players that were entered into communication pairs that they did not inherently know their partner's alignment, but I decided against it because I didn't want to influence any wolf plans to trick human players. This seems to have worked out well for Angrynarwhal, but not for Dr.Agon, and I'm not sure whether I would do it differently in a similar situation. Possibly it would be a better idea in the end, though, especially before the connecting mechanism was made clear to disconnected wolves.

There were a few player decisions that confused me a bit (for instance, that Iron never connected himself to Valex, despite knowing his alignment). I'm not sure how things would have been different otherwise.

Possibly the funniest moment in the game for me was when Valex guarded Dr.Agon after he had been lynched.

N3 role changes came about because I realized in retrospect that I basically had not given roles to 3 players. Whoops.

The yellow role came from the role "hider" I encountered on a different forum (where it was actually considered "vanilla"). I think it's a cool role that requires some interesting strategy, especially when played by a human. Potentially very powerful, but with a p big risk.

Anyways, yeah. Hope a few careless things didn't fuck stuff up too much. I might have had other thoughts but I don't remember what they are offhand. Ah well.

Title: Re: TOTALLY NORMAL TWG: SKIDIDOOP - GAME OVER M&Ms WIN
Post by: eep on February 11, 2013, 09:36:06 PM
Quote from: Dietcar on February 11, 2013, 07:21:48 PM
I only briefly read through the roles, but it didn't seem to me like the skittles realistically had a chance with a 7-5 player split. Even though the M&Ms started off disconnected/similarly uninformed, once skittles started dying, there just weren't enough players working in the interest of the skittles to figure things out.

That said, I liked the flavor a lot, and it was a well-appreciated effort.
See, I'm not 100% convinced that it WAS such a guaranteed wolf victory under those starting parameters. I didn't realize that penut/angrynarwhal didn't feel confident about k// being a wolf, which admittedly could have changed a few things (and possibly ended things in a tie). So possibly I should have just let the game continue out to the end, but even if it hadn't been, there were a lot of possible ways for things to end. If penut had been lynched instead of AJ, it's quite likely that k// would have gone along with a "let all of my wolf partners die and then use my vote priority" plan, which would, of course, have ended in Trientalis exploding and taking him with her. Furthermore, while it was really obvious from outside of the game which players were wolves and how many there were, I think a lot of the actual M&Ms felt the risk of connecting, even with someone they THOUGHT were on their team, a lot more keenly.

If I were to redo this game, I would probably have the mechanism (wolves do not all know the identity of other wolves) and the bonding role be known publicly, which would allow humans more freedom to manipulate it. Possibly would also get rid of the provision in human hider that kills them when they hide behind a wolf, or added in something similar to the wolf hider.

It was also unfair of me to say that humans played especially poorly - mostly, penut just caused a LOT of chaos which kept people from noticing the obvious, so kudos to him for doing something i would have thought impossible.
